    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_327266152" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/327266152" />
    <a title="Karo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1416636-karo"><img alt="Karo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451918260p2/1416636.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/327266152?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karo" href="/user/show/1416636-karo">Karo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783570127759" href="/book/show/1733346.Das_Amulett_von_Samarkand">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416636-karo?shelf=language-german">language-german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416636-karo?shelf=fantasy-o-sci-fi">fantasy-o-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416636-karo?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer327266152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1414368640814786131">I was rather sceptical towards this book at first. I was expecting to get a cheap and uninspired Harry Potter-copy but this book, in fact, doesn't have much in common with JK Rowling's popular saga. <br/><br/>This book description here sums things up very well:<br/>"Nathaniel is a magician's apprentice, taking his first lessons in the arts of magic. But when a devious hot-shot wizard named Simon Lovelace ruthlessly humiliates Nathaniel in front of his elders, Nathaniel decides to kick up his education a few no</span>
  <span id="freeText1414368640814786131" style="display:none">I was rather sceptical towards this book at first. I was expecting to get a cheap and uninspired Harry Potter-copy but this book, in fact, doesn't have much in common with JK Rowling's popular saga. <br /><br />This book description here sums things up very well:<br />"Nathaniel is a magician's apprentice, taking his first lessons in the arts of magic. But when a devious hot-shot wizard named Simon Lovelace ruthlessly humiliates Nathaniel in front of his elders, Nathaniel decides to kick up his education a few notches and show Lovelace who's boss. With revenge on his mind, he summons the powerful djinni, Bartimaeus. But summoning Bartimaeus and controlling him are two different things entirely, and when Nathaniel sends the djinni out to steal Lovelace's greatest treasure, the Amulet of Samarkand, he finds himself caught up in a whirlwind of magical espionage, murder, and rebellion." <br /><br />I love this new approach and definition of being a "wizard" here in Stroud's world: Wizards don't perform magic themselves. They need to summon demons like Djinn, Foliot, Imps, Afrits or Marids to do so.<br /><br />And that's were the trouble really begins because those demons are vicious things, trying to trick or harm their masters whereever they can. It so happens with Nathaniel and Bartimaeus. <br /><br />The story itself takes quite a while before it really kicks off and there are some rather dragging parts in between as well, but the POVs of Nathaniel and Bartimaeus really make up for this because they are just <i>hilarious</i>! <br /><br />The Amulet of Samarkand is darker and the characters are a lot more snarky and edgy than, for example, JK Rowling's characters. The book is full of funny remarks and potshots. <br />(I have to say though that I'm <i>NOT</i> a fan of the footnotes. They <i>are</i> funny but I found them really distracting as they interrupt the flow of the narrative.)<br /><br />The highlight of the book is, without any doubt, the love-hate relationship of Nathaniel and Bartimaeus and it was so heartwarming when Bartimaeus told Nathaniel at the end of the book that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he has everything it takes to be a great wizard and that he should always be careful and take care of himself... awwww!!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br />I really became a fan of their relationship!<br /><br />The book has a really great showdown that I could envision all the way through. <br /><br />All in all, the book is a real fun ride and I'm curious to see where the second book will be taking us!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1414368640814786131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9371994-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461856985p2/9371994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/411168393?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/9371994-allison">Allison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

  </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=series-complete">series-complete</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=award-winner">award-winner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=witches-wizards-mages">witches-wizards-mages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=review-freebie">review-freebie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=setting-britain-ireland">setting-britain-ireland</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=published-2000s">published-2000s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer411168393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14435843980754384493"><i>The Amulet of Samarkand</i> is set in a modern-day London that is ruled by Magicians. It is written from the perspective of a djinni (demon) and an undervalued magician's apprentice. The plot is clever, and the dual POV take on magical power struggles is unique. The problem is, I didn't like any of the characters. The djinni came the closest because he's an interesting character with a sense of humor, but the boy... I didn't like him at all, and he's the most sympathetic human character we meet (I d</span>
  <span id="freeText14435843980754384493" style="display:none"><i>The Amulet of Samarkand</i> is set in a modern-day London that is ruled by Magicians. It is written from the perspective of a djinni (demon) and an undervalued magician's apprentice. The plot is clever, and the dual POV take on magical power struggles is unique. The problem is, I didn't like any of the characters. The djinni came the closest because he's an interesting character with a sense of humor, but the boy... I didn't like him at all, and he's the most sympathetic human character we meet (I don't feel I can count the female caretakers since they are so removed from the reader).<br /><br />Aside from not liking the characters, I also struggled to connect with them at all. The narration was very focused on what happened from an external vantage-point. Even the djinni's adventures, told in first-person, were still very remote. It felt very like a Middle-grade novel that a young boy might enjoy without missing the character development or the internal dialogue. That said, I think the themes make this more YA, so it should have offered a little more sophistication. <br /><br />However it should be classified, mentally I could appreciate the plot, but something deeper was lacking and I couldn't really get into it myself. Maybe it's just that I don't enjoy these types of books geared more towards boys (I also struggled with <i>The Lightning Thief</i> and the <i>Bobby Pendragon</i> series), but I kept taking a break to read something more satisfying. <br /><br /><i>**Received free arc for review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14435843980754384493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HjjkWlKtAnHmHrhc9HzYaZ6iBgayIfsjhdbFasHQQaUkHo2I6fPLGUE1DD0DidK2SP3hznysdUTeqIPbDJOzPw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vhcL2HYl4zDtzDhPOcl8PpEbuktMM3ON9AQGAU7XWU+EMWIKzXsqWErnjC7OPHbhR0Rdg4K+/eqvekCwg5Sr1Q==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer275047694078709384">Jonathan Anthony Stroud is an author of fantasy books, mainly for children and youths.<br/><br/>Stroud grew up in St Albans where he enjoyed reading books, drawing pictures, and writing stories. Between the ages seven and nine he was often ill, so he spent most of his days in the hospital or in his bed at home. To escape boredom he would occupy himself with books and stories. After he completed his studies </span>
  <span id="freeText275047694078709384" style="display:none">Jonathan Anthony Stroud is an author of fantasy books, mainly for children and youths.<br /><br />Stroud grew up in St Albans where he enjoyed reading books, drawing pictures, and writing stories. Between the ages seven and nine he was often ill, so he spent most of his days in the hospital or in his bed at home. To escape boredom he would occupy himself with books and stories. After he completed his studies of English literature at the University of York, he worked in London as an editor for the Walker Books store. He worked with different types of books there and this soon led to the writing of his own books. During the 1990s, he started publishing his own works and quickly gained success.<br /><br />In May 1999, Stroud published his first children's novel, Buried Fire, which was the first of a line of fantasy/mythology children's books.<br /><br />Among his most prominent works are the bestselling Bartimaeus Trilogy. A special feature of these novels compared to others of their genre is that Stroud examines the stereotypes and ethics of the magician class and the enslaved demons. This is done by examining the perspective of the sarcastic and slightly egomaniacal djinni Bartimaeus. The books in this series are The Amulet of Samarkand, The Golem's Eye, and Ptolemy's Gate, his first books to be published in the United States. <br /><br />Stroud lives in St Albans, Hertfordshire, with his two children, Isabelle and Arthur, and his wife Gina, an illustrator of children's books.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="275047694078709384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
